**VI.2.1. News articles**


Of the 157 news articles in the sample, 56.05% are from _Eldiario.es_, 21.02% from _El Mundo_, another

14.01% from _Elconfidencial.com_, and only 8.92% from _El País_. The native digital outlets

total 110 news articles, 70.06%, while the traditional outlets account for 29.94%

with 47 publications in this genre.

|TABLE OF DATA ON NEWS ARTICLES BY OUTLET|Col2|Col3|
|---|---|---|
|**Outlet**|**Number of news articles**|**Percentage (%)**|
|_El Mundo_ |33|21.0|
|_El País_ |14|8.9|
|_Elconfidencial.com_ |22|14.0|
|_Eldiario.es_ |88|56.1|
|Total|157|100.0|


The difference between the news articles published by the two digital outlets is 42.04%,

with _Eldiario.es_ publishing four times as many as _Elconfidencial.com_. For its part, _El Mundo_ had

more than double the publications of _El País_ in this genre, with a difference of 12.1% between

the number of news articles published by both outlets.


When observing the number of news articles published by outlet across the selected

periods, again _Eldiario.es_ is seen as the outlet that most influences the general

trend of news articles.

|TABLE OF DATA ON NEWS ARTICLES PUBLISHED BY OUTLET OVER TIME|Col2|Col3|Col4|Col5|Col6|Col7|Col8|
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
|**Outlet**|**Month 1**|**Month 2**|**Month****3 **|**Month 4**|**Month****5 **|**Month 6**|**Totals**|
|_Eldiario.es_|16|6|8|15|12|31|88|
|_Elconfidencial.com_|3|0|0|0|3|16|22|
|_El Mundo_|4|2|5|7|6|9|33|
|_El País_|2|0|3|1|4|4|14|
|Total|25|8 |16|23|25|60|157|


|PERCENTAGE TREND OF NEWS ARTICLES PUBLISHED BY OUTLET OVER TIME|Col2|Col3|Col4|Col5|Col6|
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
|**Trend**|**Months 1-****2 **|**Months 2-3**|**Months 3-4**|**Months 4-****5 **|**Months 5-****6 **|
|**General (Total)**|-68%|+100%|+43.75%|8.69%|140%|
|**_Eldiario.es_ **|-62.5%|+33.33%|+87.5%|-20%|158.33%|
|**_Elconfidencial.com_ **|-300%|Stable|Stable|300%|433.33%|
|**_El Mundo_ **|-50%|+150%|+40%|-14.28%|+50%|
|**_El País_ **|-200%|+300%|-66.66%%|300%|Stable|


All outlets decreased their volume of news between the first and second period,

while between the second and third they rose, with the exception of _Elconfidencial.com_, which

remained without publishing on this topic. Between the third and fourth period the

influence of _Eldiario.es_ on the overall upward trend is more evident, since _Elconfidencial.com_ remained

stable without publications and _El País_ reduced the number of news pieces: only _El Mundo_

joined in the increase in quantities, although its 7 publications are less than half

those of _Eldiario.es_. However, between the fourth and fifth period there is an upturn in the

general trend that does not correspond to the number of news articles published by

_Eldiario.es_, making it the only period in which its influence was not predominant

in the total sample.


**VI.2.1.1. By authorship**


Of the 157 news articles published, 45 are from the EFE agency, 27 from EUROPA PRESS (EP) and 1

was created from several agency news items, totaling 73 publications. For their part,

each outlet claimed authorship of 35 news articles from the total: 17 from _Eldiario.es_, 9 from _El Mundo_, 5

from _El País_ and 4 from _Elconfidencial.com_. Two news articles attributed to allied outlets stood out: 1

from _Asturias 24_ and 1 from _La Palma Ahora_, both published by _Eldiario.es_. This leaves a total

of 47 news articles with nominal authorship.


If we look at the total news articles published by outlet according to authorship, of the 73

agency publications, 44 are from _Eldiario.es_: 21 from EFE and 23 from EP. Another outlet with

diverse agency publications was _El Mundo_ which, of a total of 15, 11 were from EFE and 4

from EP, while all 13 agency news items from _Elconfidencial.com_ belonged to

EFE. _El País_ has a total of only one agency publication, whose authorship it attributes to

"agencies," implying that it was composed of information from several different agencies.

On the other hand, of the 47 nominal authorships, _Eldiario.es_ has 25, _El Mundo_ 9, and _El_

_País_ and _Elconfidencial.com_ 5 each.

the journalist from _Eldiario.es_, Alicia Avilés Pozo, is the author with the greatest number of

publications with 4 news articles. She is followed by 6 journalists with two publications each: Adolf

Beltran, Diego Jimeno Manrique, and María José Alarcón from _Eldiario.es_, Marta Belber from _El_

_Mundo_, Elisa Silió from _El País_, and Miguel Ayuso from _Elconfidencial.com_.

**VI.2.1.2. By sources**


Of the 157 news articles in the sample, 131 directly reproduced the interested

information of the source, which is more than 80% of the news articles in the sample. Among the 131

news articles with interested sources, 93 came from representatives or communiqués of some political

party and 1 was a reproduction of the programmed content of one of these, so the

use of political parties as direct sources of news represented more than 68% of

total news publications with direct interested sources, which in turn represents

almost 60% of the total news articles in the entire sample. A total of 24 news articles used some

public institution as an interested source, while only 13 reproduced the interests of

some private institution.


The political party with the greatest number of direct reproductions in news articles was the PP,

with 32 news articles using a spokesperson from this party as the article's source. The

PSOE was the next party with the greatest number of direct reproductions as a source in

news articles, with 26 publications. In numbers it is followed by Podemos with 10 news articles, although

if we add the total of the confluences with which the purple party ran that year (En

Comú Podem and Ahora Madrid), it had a total of 12 news articles reproducing it as an

interested political source.


The next party in numbers was Compromís, with 6 news articles, while the PNV was

reproduced in 4 articles. Ciudadanos and Geroa Bai were reproduced 3 times each.

There were also news articles with reproduction of mixed interested political sources: one article

reproducing spokespeople from the PP and the PNV, another from the PSOE and IU, and another from the PP and the PSOE.


If we break down this data by outlet, it stands out that the only outlet reproducing

interested sources from Podemos was _Eldiario.es_. It is also notable that the PP was reproduced

about 14 times by this outlet, 10 by _El Mundo_, and 4 each in _Elconfidencial.com_ and _El_

_País_, which is very striking if we take into account that _Eldiario.es_ is an outlet with

an editorial line adverse to the PP. However, if we look at the number of direct reproductions

of the PSOE by outlet, we find that _Eldiario.es_ exceeded in 4 units the number of

direct reproductions it made of the PP: its 18 news articles were followed by _El Mundo_ (4),

_Elconfidencial.com_ (2) and _El País_ (2).


Notable are the few reproductions of the PSOE in _El País_, an outlet that used to have a

more favorable editorial line toward this party in previous years, as well as the fact that it

published no news article reproducing any "spokesperson" for Compromís, Podemos and the

confluences, and IU: it only published spokespeople from bipartisan parties, Ciudadanos, and the PNV.


own.

own.


These anomalies could be explained by quantifying the number of news articles reproducing

interested sources from political parties that originate from an agency news item. Thus, of

the 14 news articles reproducing interested sources from the PP in Eldiario.es, 10 of them originate

from agencies (6 from EFE and 4 from EP), while 4 are of their own production: 2 signed by the

editorial staff and 2 by their authors. If we analyze journalistic narratives from this perspective,

one can appreciate just from the headlines how an excess of agency news

ends up positioning spokespeople who are not usually highlighted by the editorial line of this outlet (Table

16):

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|
|Ayllón says no government has tackled such a strong anti-corruption agenda|EFE|José Luis Ayllón|
|Ayllón assures that Spain is halfway through the reforms it needs|EFE|José Luis Ayllón|
|Becerril advocates transparency and spending controls to prevent corruption|EFE|Soledad Becerril|
|Sáenz de Santamaría challenges critics to rebut the ten-point list of improvements facilitated by the 2016 PGE|EFE|Soraya Sáenz deSantamaría|
|Montoro says public administration has overcome Larra's curse: Fortunately nothing remains|EP|José AlbertoMartín-Toledano|
|Cifuentes joins the Madrid City Council plan for Ifema|EP|Cristina Cifuentes|
|PP chides PSOE for requesting funds for Historical Memory while supporting an antisemitic Podemos with civil-war-style proclamations|EP|Pedro Gómez de laSerna |
|PP will be maximally demanding on transparency despite leaving its law unapproved|_Eldiario.es_ |PP Castilla LaMancha|


own.


In all the headlines with agency authorship in Table 16, _Eldiario.es_ directly reproduced

the interests of some spokesperson who made the declarations, whereas in the news article with

own authorship the outlet attempts to downplay the declaration by the PP of Castilla-La Mancha by

publishing it alongside a direct criticism of the party in the same headline. However, if we

perform the same exercise of headline analysis with news articles from interested sources of the PSOE in

this outlet, the differences in news treatment of articles with own authorship compared

to those from agencies are not as evident (Table 17).

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|
|Canary Islands government begins process to regulate revolving doors  |EFE|Aarón Afonso|

Own production.


The same tendency seen in the headlines of news articles with interested PSOE sources can

be observed in those with interested articles from Compromís, PODEMOS and the

confluences. In this case it was also possible to observe how a headline with own authorship

from _Eldiario.es_ was used to criticize Ciudadanos in a way quite similar to that seen in Table

14 in the own-authored article from _Eldiario.es_ under the headline "PP will be maximally demanding

on transparency despite leaving its law unapproved." In the example in Table

18, _Eldiario.es_ criticizes the abstention of Ciudadanos on the proposed Open Accounts Law

of Extremadura:

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|
|Podemos presents a law for total transparency of the administration|EFE|PODEMOS deputies|
|Podemos promotes an Open Accounts Law to prevent corruption|EFE|PODEMOS deputies|
|Podemos proposes measures to remove from office those who fail to fulfill their electoral commitments|EP|Juantxo López de Uralde|
|Victoria Anderica: I am going to create an ordinance requiring maximum information to be provided|_Eldiario.es_|Victoria Anderica|
|Alcaraz guarantees the independence and professionalism of the Transparency Council|_Eldiario.es_|Conseller de Transparencia|
|Passed, with C's abstaining, the proposed Open Accounts Law |_Eldiario.es_ |Álvaro Jaén|


Confluences in _Eldiario.es_. Own production.


Although in the examples seen the differences in treatment or stance are observed from

the headlines, in the majority of articles they are detected in the body of the news item, as

we will see in the section dedicated to thematic analysis. However, starting solely from

the headlines of news articles in relation to their authorship, source, and political spokespeople, we can

say that the anomaly seen in _El País_ does not occur due to a situation similar to that of _Eldiario.es_:

_El País_ has only one agency news article, so unlike _Eldiario.es_, it does not position

political spokespeople not usually highlighted in its editorial line due to an excess of agency news

articles. In the case of _El Mundo_, of the 5 news articles with own authorship, 4

directly reproduce PP "spokespeople" as an interested source and 1 from the PNV: 80% and 20%

respectively (Table 19).

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|
|Unanimity for transparency in the Provincial Government|_El Mundo_|PP deputies|
|Transparency and Participation regulations opened to citizens|_El Mundo_|Luis Martínez|
|European provinces sign good governance commitment in Castellón|_El Mundo_|Javier Moliner|
|Moliner seeks maximum consensus in drafting the Transparency Law|_El Mundo_ |Javier Moliner|


own.


If we compare these political "spokespeople" with the 6 agency news articles from _El Mundo_, both the

PP and Compromís are reproduced 33.33% and the PSOE 16.66%, leaving a

majority to the PP if we take into account that the mixed spokespeople are Basque deputies from the PP and

PNV: dividing the 16.66% of the mixed "spokesperson" in two would leave the PNV at 8.33% and the PP

at a total of 41.66%. This means that, both in agency news articles and in the

outlet's own, _El Mundo_ shows a predominance of certain spokespersons (PP and PNV),

so there are no discrepancies between the political spokespeople positioned according to their authorship in

relation to its editorial line. Agency news articles contributed greater diversity of interested sources

in the news of this traditional outlet (Table 20).

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|Col3|SOURCE|SPOKESPERSON|

own.


On the part of _Elconfidencial.com_, of the 7 news articles with interested "spokespeople" from political

parties, 5 are from the EFE agency, with 4 from the PP and 1 from the PSOE. The rest of the news articles with

this type of declaration have 1 nominal authorship and 1 from the outlet itself, each reproducing

the PSOE and Ahora Madrid, respectively. However, the tendencies in the headlines of

these last two news articles maintain the same editorial line presented by the set of

agency news articles that reproduce interested declarations from the PP, since those of the PSOE and

Ahora Madrid were used to generate suspicion toward these last two

political formations.

|HEADLINE|AUTHOR|SOURCE|SPOKESPERSON|
|---|---|---|---|
|Montoro assures that diligence has been exercised regarding Arístegui and G. Serna  |EFE|CristobalMontoro|PP|
|Santamaría highlights the speed of the Conflicts Office investigating Arístegui  |EFE|Soraya Sáenz deSanta María|PP|
|Posada recommends that De la Serna withdraw his candidacy for Congress|EFE|Jesús Posada|PP|
|Spain awarded in France for reform of its Public Administration|EFE|Ramón deMiguel|PP|
|Page does not rule out criminal proceedings over Villa's expenses with RTVCM cards|EFE|EmilianoGarcía-Page|PSOE|
|PP councilor for Festivals in Marbella spent 14,600 euros on telephone in one month|Javier Porcuna|Amparo de laGama|PSOE|
|Carmena admits making two cash payments of 60,000 euros|_Elconfidencial.com_ |ManuelaCarmena|AhoraMadrid|


own.


Of the 24 news articles with direct reproduction of interested sources from public institutions,

10 were from _Eldiario.es_, 6 from _El Mundo_, 5 from _Elconfidencial.com_, and 3 from _El País_. Of the 10 from

_Eldiario.es_, only one had own authorship and 9 were from agencies: 7 from EFE and 2 from EP. In the case of

the 6 from _El Mundo_, 2 were nominal and 4 from agencies: 3 from EFE and 1 from EP. Of the 5

news articles from _Elconfidencial.com_, 4 were from the EFE agency and 1 nominal, while of the 3

news articles from _El País_, 2 were nominal and 1 of its own production.


In the majority of these news articles there was no great difference between the news treatment of

articles with agency authorship compared to those signed by the outlets' own journalists and by the

editorial staff: communiqués and declarations from public entities were mixed with

information from websites of parliaments, provincial councils, and public offices alike. Thus,

publications of salaries, budgets, and court rulings were used as sources in

news articles where transparency and good governance was in some way the main topic

and, in many cases, served as institutional propaganda (Table 22).

|HEADLINE|OUTLET|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|---|
|The King calls for transparency in companies in its broadest sense|_El País_|MiquelAlberola|Felipe VI|
|The Assembly will designate a tribunal to oversee good public management|_El País_|Elisa Silió|Asamblea deMadrid|
|Manacor City Council members will not receive per diems or accept gifts|_El Mundo_|EFE|Joan Llodrà Gayà|
|Councilors' income will be public|_El Mundo_|MartaBelber|Ayuntamiento deMadrid|
|The Orfeón Pamplonés will publish external audit reports on its website as part of a Transparency Plan|_Eldiario.es_|EP|Orfeón Pamplonés|
|Waiting lists have lost ten thousand patients in November, according to the regional government|_Eldiario.es_|_Eldiario.es_|Regina Leal(SESCAM)|
|The CNMV believes Spain is at the vanguard on corporate governance|_Elconfidencial.com_|EFE|CNMV|
|The judge sets bail at the 16 million charged by Abengoa's leadership|_Elconfidencial.com_ |EFE|AudienciaNacional|


As can be observed, in the majority of news articles with interested spokespeople from

public institutions there was not much difference between the news treatment by authorship:

both nominal authorship (signed by a journalist), the outlet's own (signed by the

editorial staff), and agency authorship alike served to promote the institution itself or, in

some cases, the Spanish government and Spanish companies. However, four news articles from the

native-digital outlets differed from this majority by having the Transparency

Council or its then-president, Esther Arismendi, as a source. In this regard, the 3 news articles

from _Eldiario.es_ with EFE authorship and the one from _Elconfidencial.com_ with nominal authorship criticized

the government, the opposition, and the culture of transparency in public administration.

|HEADLINE|OUTLET|AUTHOR|SOURCE|
|---|---|---|---|
|The culture of transparency does not exist in Spain. We need to change the mentality|_Elconfidencial.com_|JesúsEscudero|Consejo deTransparencia|
|The president of the Transparency Council denounces difficulties and lack of resources|_Eldiario.es_|EFE|EstherArismendi|
|The president of the Transparency Council says she has no boss as an opposition accuses her of covering for the Government|_Eldiario.es_|EFE|EstherArismendi|
|The Transparency Council criticizes the Government's intent to restrict information on public salaries|_Eldiario.es_ |EFE|EstherArismendi|


In these articles the type of authorship does not imply a change in news treatment, so

we can confirm that, in news articles with interested sources from public institutions,

it is the source and not the authorship that can change the outlet's informational tendency. In the

case of the 13 news articles with interested sources from private institutions, 7 were from agencies:

6 from EFE and one from EP, which strongly influenced the informational contrast that some

outlets sought to present on their media agenda.


Of the 6 news articles from _Elconfidencial.com_, 2 had nominal authorship, 1 from the outlet itself, and 3 from the EFE agency; of the 5 publications from _Eldiario.es_, 2 were from EFE, 1 from EP, and

two nominal, while _El Mundo_'s sole news article was from the EFE agency. In the case

of _El País_, with also only one news article reproducing interests from private institution sources,

its publication was an open letter signed by CSIC scientists addressed to

the supposed future president of the institution. In it, signed by "scientists and

professionals in science" who work, have worked, or are affiliated with the CSIC, they demanded

a change in the institution according to the transparency parameters cited in Ley 19/2013:


"Under your leadership and direction, we aspire to definitively consolidate the maturity that the

public science and technology system must achieve as befits a

free, democratic, plural and open society… The current structure and functioning of the CSIC does not

promote excellence, but rather naturalizes an institutional model anchored in an

obsolete archetype of centralized and bureaucratized administration" (González-Ruibal et al.,

2015).


With the exception of an item from _Eldiario.es_ titled "Biscaytik brings together municipal

representatives and experts in a conference on data protection at the local level" (EP,

2015), in which the EP agency reproduced a training conference by the Fundación

BiscayTIK that sought to overcome possible discrepancies between the LOPD and the

transparency law in the Basque context, the majority of interested sources from private institutions

contained a reclamatory charge on issues of institutional or

corporate transparency.


Thus, the only news article with these characteristics from _El Mundo_, with EFE authorship, was

based on the secretary of Social Protection and Public Policies of the Confederación Sindical de

Comisiones Obreras (CCOO), Carlos Bravo, to denounce inequalities and lack of

transparency in high-ranking positions of the IBEX. Similarly, the EFE agency reproduced

complaints from the Plataforma de Afectados por Hepatitis C in 1 news item from _Eldiario.es_ and another from

_Elconfidencial.com_, as well as from the Organización Médico Colegial in _Eldiario.es_: the 3

publications highlighted the lack of funding, discrimination, and non-compliance with the plan

developed by the Ministry of Health to treat this disease. The Spanish agency

also reproduced complaints from Transparencia Internacional in 1 publication from

_Elconfidencial.com_ and another from the Asociación Española de Accionistas Minoritarios de

Empresas Cotizadas against the Board of Directors of Abengoa in the same outlet,

so its influence on items with privately interested sources was felt in

the news of the sample outlets that sought to act as a counterpower on certain

topics.


Although we can confirm that agencies had a significant influence on the

reproduction of private source interests in the sample outlets and that, moreover,

these tended to be NGOs, professional or citizen groups seeking to influence

public opinion, the fact that these news articles represented just over 8% of total

news articles indicates that this counterpower effect meant very little in the total.


If we analyze the type of authors by grouping them into news agencies, nominal authors of

the outlet, and the outlet's own authorship, crossing the data with the type of source, in turn grouped

into "spokespeople" from private institutions, public institutions, and political parties, it becomes much

clearer how in the total of 131 news articles with "spokespeople" from interested sources, the

predominance of political party sources was the majority across all types of

authorship.


Also observed is a clear imbalance between news articles using sources from

public institutions and private ones, with the former double the latter. In fact,

the intention to exercise counterpower from the outlets was fulfilled in news items signed

by journalists at the outlets (the nominal authors).

|TABLE OF DATA FOR GRAPH 16|Col2|Col3|Col4|Col5|Col6|
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
|||**Spokesperson**|**Spokesperson**|**Spokesperson**|Total|
|||Privateinstitution|Publicinstitution|Politicalparty|Politicalparty|
|**Authorship**|Agencies|7|17|39|63|
|**Authorship**|Allied outlet|0|0|2|2|
|**Authorship**|Nominal|5|5|25|35|
|**Authorship**|Own outlet|1|2|28|31|
|**Total**|**Total**|13|24|94|131|


Of the 26 news articles not directly reproducing interested sources, 14 are from _Eldiario.es_, 6 from

_El Mundo_, 4 from _Elconfidencial.com_, and 2 from _El País_. Of the 14 from _Eldiario.es_, 7 were from

agencies, 5 had nominal authorship, and 2 were from the outlet itself, while _El Mundo_ had 4

nominal authorships, 2 from agencies, and none of its own. _Elconfidencial.com_ had 2 own

authorships, 1 nominal, and 1 from agencies, while _El País_ had only 2 nominal authorships. In

this case, agency news articles only significantly influenced _Eldiario.es_ with

50% of authorships, since in _El Mundo_ they represented 33.33%, in _Elconfidencial.com_

25%, and in _El País_, agencies had no representation whatsoever.


Of the 26 news articles not reproducing interested sources, 14 have multiple sources, showing

informational contrast in 4 publications with agency authorship, 2 from the outlets themselves, and 8

nominal. This means that 66.66% of news articles with nominal authorship were produced

with multiple sources, while in own-outlet authorships the use of these sources

represents 50%, and in the case of agency news articles, 40%.


Among the 12 news articles without multiple sources, one nominal authorship used as source the website

of the lower house of Congress to denounce how an impeached and dismissed deputy

continued receiving a salary. Another 2 nominal authorships used drafts that made visible

political intentions to change the situation of transparency in Spain, taking its

inadequacy for granted: a draft ordinance from the Madrid City Council and the Code of Ethics and Good

Governance of Valencia. The inadequacy of the law was also highlighted by Marta Peirano

(2015) with the net neutrality measures proposed at the _Free Culture Forum 2015_

(#FCForum2015) by noting that "the Transparency Law does not include any measure for

whistleblowers." The Transparency Law was used as a source in an agency news item

published in _Eldiario.es_ and another with own authorship from _Elconfidencial.com_, while the

transparency portal was used as a source in 4 agency news items (3 published in

_Eldiario.es_ and 1 in _Elconfidencial.com_). Finally, _El Mundo_ published an EP news item that

used as its source the governing pact signed in the Balearic Islands in 2015.
own.


If we set aside news articles with agency authorship and those with multiple sources, it stands out

how the three sample outlets that had data units at the time sought to influence

the politics and public policies on transparency affecting journalism: the native

digital outlets did so with their own-authored news items while _El Mundo_ did so in an

article signed by Marta Belber (2015). In this regard, in the article by _Eldiario.es_

(2015a) titled "El Portal de la Transparencia del gobierno se actualiza 24 horas después de

una información de _Eldiario.es_," the native digital highlighted that thanks to its counterpower role,

the government was compelled to comply with the Transparency Law by publishing on the transparency portal

that four former government members had left public service to join the private sector:


"This Sunday we reported that the Transparency Portal had not updated data

on the monitoring of senior government officials since January. That is, the

controls on 'revolving doors' between government and the private sector required by

the Transparency Law were not being kept up to date. Just 24 hours after our story, the Government

reacted and updated said data." (_Eldiario.es_, 2015)


Despite being a news article that self-promotes the outlet and calls for

the enrollment of more subscribers, it is still striking how for this outlet transparency and

good governance is a fundamental topic for exerting pressure on the politics and public policies

affecting the exercise of journalism, and it attempts to capitalize on this to gain more users. In

a similar way, _Elconfidencial.com_ positioned among the 10 most important items of

December 10, 2015 the entry into force of the transparency law in city councils and

autonomous communities that year, denouncing that by then "the majority of

regional governments have not created the bodies that must ensure the correct application of all the

precepts of the Transparency Law and that will have to manage citizen complaints on this matter" (_Elconfidencial.com_, 2015a). As in the last news item

cited from _Eldiario.es_, it used the transparency portal as a source.


In _El Mundo_, the news item by Marta Belber (2015) titled "Los concejales de Madrid sólo

podrán reunirse con 'lobbies' identificados" was based on the draft ordinance from the

Madrid City Council to highlight measures intended to "regulate revolving doors

between politics and private business," such as the lobbying register and fines of up to 30,000

euros for officials who circumvent this regulation. That a news item with nominal authorship from

_El Mundo_ was published with a favorable tendency toward Ahora Madrid is a

noteworthy fact if we take into consideration that, given the editorial line of this outlet, no

article was published reproducing interested sources from Podemos and the confluences—the

sole exception to reproducing interested sources from the PP, PSOE, and PNV were two articles from

EFE (2015a; 2015b) that reproduced a source from Compromís of the Valencia government,

where the PSOE governs in coalition. As in the last example from _Eldiario.es_, _El_

_Mundo_ also took advantage of open data to denounce political actions: in an

article from September 13, 2015 titled "El imputado Zarrías seguirá hasta febrero

cobrando del Congreso" (Becerro, 2015), it made use of the lower house of

Congress website to denounce that national deputy Gaspar Zarrías (PSOE), who had

resigned in July after the Supreme Court confirmed his indictment in the

ERE case, was still receiving taxpayer money.


Of the 14 news articles without reproduction of interested sources but with multiple sources, the authorship of

the 8 from _Eldiario.es_ was 3 from agencies, 4 nominal, and 1 from the outlet itself. _El Mundo_ had

one news item from the EFE agency and another signed by Andrés Corpas, while

_Elconfidencial.com_ had one from the outlet itself and another by David Fernández. For its part, _El_

_País_ published 2 nominal news items: one by Elisa Silió and another by Ivanna Vallespín.


Of the 4 agency news articles without reproduction of interested sources but with multiple sources, 3

were published by _Eldiario.es_: 1 from EFE and 2 from EP. The two EP news items announced the

first appearance of the president of the Transparency and Good Governance Council,

Esther Arizmendi, before Congress. These news items were written differently

by _Eldiario.es_ from the same agency information, which signals an

interest on this outlet's part in making visible the events prior to the appearance that would dissociate

the governing party from transparency initiatives: "She herself requested to appear before

parliament after the PP vetoed the PSOE's request for her to be summoned to

inform the Chamber of the allocation of three million euros that the Council

will have in the next fiscal year" (EP, 2015b).


In another news item with these characteristics from the EFE agency, published by this native digital

under the headline "Afonso reconoce la falta de medios humanos y materiales en la administración

de Justicia canaria" (EFE, 2015c), declarations were contrasted from various Canary Islands politicians

from the PP, PSOE, and Podemos who used transparency as a weapon against

opposing political formations. Finally, the last of the agency news items without

reproduction of interested sources but with multiple sources was published by _El Mundo_ under the

title "Presidencia aumenta presupuesto del CNI por amenaza del terrorismo yihadista" with the

authorship of EFE (2015d). This news item, although it amplified the appearance of the undersecretary of

the Presidency, Federico Ramos (PP), before the Budget Committee of the Congress of

Deputies, was nonetheless an example of some outlets seeking to position

transparency and good governance as a main topic on the media agenda: the contrast of

multiple sources positioned all deputies and spokespeople who used transparency

as a banner to attack opposing political representatives.


Of the 8 news articles without reproduction of interested sources, with multiple sources and nominal

authorship, 4 were from _Eldiario.es_, 2 from _El País_, 1 from _Elconfidencial.com_, and 1 from _El Mundo_. In

these, a difference in news treatment was seen between native digital and

traditional outlets.


In the news item by Ivanna Vallespín (2015) that _El País_ published on July 2, 2015 under the

title "Mas declara 400.000 euros en ahorros y acciones," the income, tax, and asset declarations

that members of the Catalan Generalitat

published on their regional transparency portal were presented in detail, contrasted with official

sources from the regional entity. The other nominal news item from _El País_, by Elisa Silió (2015) and under the

headline "La Asamblea designará un tribunal que vele por la buena gestión pública," positioned

how deputies from the Community of Madrid were battling in the regional assembly to

prevent the Public Procurement Court of Madrid from being given "powers to oversee

transparency in place of the Consultative Council, which is to disappear."


These two news items from the traditional outlet showed no attempt to influence the politics or

public policies affecting transparency, although Elisa Silió did position

political battles over the designation of transparency-related posts. It was a

treatment very similar to that of the only nominal news item without reproduction of interested

sources and with multiple sources from _El Mundo_, which limited itself to recounting the various

versions of the corruption scandal of the Catalan Basketball Federation under the headline

"Presuntas prácticas corruptas" (Corpas, 2015). However, news items with these

characteristics from the native digital outlets did attempt to influence the politics and public

policies of transparency.


Articles from _Eldiario.es_ such as the one titled "De la propiedad Intelectual al estatuto de artista: la

cultura que prometen los partidos en cinco grandes hits," with shared authorship by Jaron

Rowan and Pedro Jiménez (2015a), attempted to influence the audience by exposing the PP

for its proposal of greater transparency in author rights management entities by

stating that "for this party the problem does not lie in the production model, which is obsolete and slow

to change, but in the need to re-educate citizens." The news item did this by

focusing on "how the five competing parties address the major themes that have defined

the cultural agenda in recent years, from Intellectual Property to artist subsidies." For

its part, David Fernández in _Elconfidencial.com_ attacked the management of Telemadrid carried out by

Esperanza Aguirre's PP and criticized the Community of Madrid's proposed law at the time

for lacking a spending cap, attempting to expose Ciudadanos for "not

practicing the transparency it preaches":


"Now a law-level regulation sets 600,000 euros as the ceiling. PP and C's approve

that this limit be set, if desired, by the new board of directors. Podemos wanted

300,000 as the maximum… The new director general of Telemadrid will have no spending limit."

(Fernández, 2015a)


Similarly, the only own-outlet authored news items without reproduction of interested

sources and with multiple sources belonged to the two native digital outlets in the

sample. In the news item from _Eldiario.es_ titled "Un redactor de deportes ganó más de 400.000

euros durante la época de Nacho Villa" (Eldiarioclm.es, 2015), there was an attempt to influence

public transparency policies in Castilla-La Mancha by revealing opacity in the

handling of public money related to the salaries of the former director of Radio Televisión

Castilla-La Mancha, Nacho Villa, thereby extolling the exercise of transparency carried out

through the new regional government's transparency portal:


"Radio Televisión Castilla-La Mancha has published on its new RTVCM Transparency Portal the salaries of new management positions. The reduction amounts to 11% less

than in the previous legislature." (Eldiarioclm.es, 2015)


For its part, _Elconfidencial.com_ attacked the state management of the transparency portal due to

restrictions on public information requests. In the article titled "Las trabas de

las instituciones llevan al cierre del primer portal pro-Transparencia español," the native digital

echoed a complaint from the most important transparency movements in Spain, shared

by the data journalists interviewed in this research:


"The pro-transparency organizations Access Info Europe and the Fundación Ciudadana Civio

have resolved to close indefinitely Tu Derecho a Saber, a flagship project of civil

society that they jointly managed to promote institutional

transparency in Spain. The restriction by public administrations of the right to request

information, requiring citizens to identify themselves through complex systems—such as

the digital certificate or electronic DNI—and through dozens of portals with different technical

characteristics, has motivated this decision." (Elconfidencial.com, 2015b)


**VI.2.2. Reportages**


The two native digital outlets had the most publications in this genre: of

a total of 43 reportages, _Eldiario.es_ had 16 articles and _Elconfidencial.com_ 13, together

totaling 29. The traditional outlets published 7 articles each, totaling between

them 14 reportages. The percentage ratio between the native digitals and the

traditional outlets was 67.45% in the case of the publications from _Eldiario.es_ and

_Elconfidencial.com_, and 32.46% on the part of _El Mundo_ and _El País_. This means that the

native digitals published more than double the reportages of the print-based outlets.


As can be observed, although as in the news genre _Eldiario.es_ was the

outlet with the most published articles, in reportage the differences are not as great either between

the native digital outlets or between the traditional ones. However, the difference between native

digitals and traditional outlets in reportages is similar to that recorded in news. When

looking at this data, it is also striking how the traditional outlets had the same

number of publications, given that in the news genre _El Mundo_ had more than double the

publications of _El País_.


When observing the number of news items published by outlet across the selected

periods, we see that this time it is not _Eldiario.es_ that most influences the general

trend of reportages: it published one reportage in the first month and remained the same in the

second. Another outlet that remained stable in these two periods was _El Mundo_, which

published no reportage between June 20 and July 19. However, both

_Elconfidencial.com_ and _El País_ increased the number of reportages and influenced the

general trend in these first two periods: _Elconfidencial.com_ went from publishing one

article in the first month to publishing 3 in the second, while _El País_ increased from 1 to 2.


As can be observed, _El Mundo_ published no reportage in the first two months of

the sample and then went on to publish one in the third period. The general trend between months

2 and 3 is downward for this genre; _Elconfidencial.com_ and _El País_ published 2

reportages and none, respectively.


The upturn between the third and fourth period is due to _Eldiario.es_ going from publishing no

reportage in month 3 to publishing 5 in month 4. The increase from 1 to 2 articles published by

_El Mundo_ and from 0 to 1 by _El País_ also influenced this upward trend,

while _Elconfidencial.com_ published no article in month 4.

|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
|**Outlet**|**Month 1**|**Month 2**|**Month 3**|**Month 4**|**Month 5**|**Month 6**|**Totals**|
|_Eldiario.es_ |1 |1 |0 |5 |3 |6 |16|
|_Elconfidencial.com_ |1 |3 |2 |0 |3 |4 |13|
|_El Mundo_ |0 |0 |1 |2 |1 |3 |7 |
|_El País_ |1 |2 |0 |1 |1 |2 |7 |
|Total|3 |6 |3 |8 |8 |15|43|


The stable trend between months 4 and 5 is due to the native digital outlets, while

the upturn in the general trend between the last two periods is due to each and every

one of the outlets, all of which had a spectacular increase in the number of

reportages published compared to the previous month: 200% in _Eldiario.es_, 133.33% in

_Elconfidencial.com_, 300% in _El Mundo_, and 200% in _El País_.


**VI.2.2.1.** **By authorship**


Of the 43 reportages in the sample, 37 had nominal authorship, 5 from the outlet itself, and 1 from an

agency. The percentages (Graph 22) match the nature of this journalistic genre and

its differences from news. In our sample this aspect has not deviated from the norm: the

majority authorship type in news items is from agencies and in reportage it is nominal.


Of the 37 nominal authorships, 13 were from _Eldiario.es_, 11 from _Elconfidencial.com_, 7 from

_El País_, and 6 from _El Mundo_, while of the 5 own-outlet authorships, 3 were from

_Eldiario.es_ and 2 from _Elconfidencial.com_. The single agency reportage, with EP authorship, was

published by _El Mundo_.


In the case of _Elconfidencial.com_, the outlet's own reportages are from Elconfidencial.lab.

Publications from this laboratory are usually the result of team work with the

data journalists of _Elconfidencial.com_, so this type of authorship has

importance similar to the journalistic reportages signed by one or more

members of the data journalism teams of the sample outlets.


When breaking down the total nominal authorships by outlet in reportages, we find that

the journalist from _El País_, Elena G. Sevillano, had the most publications with 3 articles in

this genre. With 2 publications she is followed by journalists Jesús Escudero and Ana Gómez

(_Elconfidencial.com_), Neus Vidal (_El País_), and Alicia Avilés Pozo (_Eldiario.es_). Of the two

articles by Neus Vidal, one was signed by him alone and another was co-signed with Oriol

Güell, who along with the rest of the nominal authorships in the reportages only published one

article in this genre (Table 26).

Although in the news genre there were 10 more articles with nominal authorship than in

reportages, in the ratio of this type of authorship to the total in each of these genres,

reportage surpassed news: nominal authorship represents 86.05% of reportages

while in news it represents 29.94%. These are figures very consistent with the

nature of both genres. Other data that stand out arise from the comparison of

journalists who wrote articles in both genres. In this regard, more than half

of the _Eldiario.es_ journalists who published reportages also published news items: six

of the eleven journalists, representing 55%. The two _El País_ journalists who also

published news represent 33.33% of the nominal authorships in reportages,

while Jesús Escudero was the only _Elconfidencial.com_ journalist to publish

articles in both genres, representing 11% of this outlet's nominal authorships in

reportages. _El Mundo_ was the only outlet without journalists who published in both

genres.

**VI.2.2.2.** **By sources**


Of the 43 reportages in the sample, 21 had multiple sources, with almost half the

publications showing evident informational contrast. The other 22 used single sources:

17 used once only and the transparency portal—national, regional, or local depending on the case—up to 5 times (Table 28).

|Source of the reportages|Type of authorship|
|---|---|

|Madrid City Council|Nominal|

|VI Expansión Financial Forum (KPMG)|Nominal|


88.37% of reportages did not directly reproduce any interested source, of which more than half had nominal authorship. 39.53% of reportages without reproduction of

interested sources are divided in two: the 11.63% that based their information on the

transparency portal and the 27.91% that based it on a single source.


Although reportages do not usually feature direct reproduction of any interested source

but rather the use of multiple sources, there were 5 reportages with direct reproduction of

interested sources: 4 from political parties and 1 from private institutions.


These interpretative narratives represent only 11.63% of the sample, which is a

notable difference from the news genre, where more than 80% directly reproduced

some interested source. The five reportages mentioned were based on a

single source from which they delved into the context of the news event, producing complete and precise

information. That was the case of one reportage that reproduced private interested sources

and four others that replicated the interests of political parties, of

which 2 reproduced a representative from Compromís, one from the PP, and the

last from one of Ciudadanos. This means that of the 43 reportages in the sample, 38 did not

directly reproduce any interested source, represented by the label "Not applicable"

for the type of "spokesperson" in Graph 24.


According to the type of authorship of these 5 reportages with direct reproduction of interested

sources, we observe that 4 of the articles had nominal authorship: 1 reproduced the

interests of KPMG [10] (_El País_), 1 of Ciudadanos (_Elconfidencial.com_), 1 of Compromís

(_Eldiario.es_) and 1 of the Murcian PP (_Eldiario.es_). _Eldiario.es_ was the only one to reproduce with

own authorship a reportage that echoed a type of interested source, which in this case

was Compromís. The "spokesperson" used in these reportages did not excessively position

political spokespersons at odds with the editorial line of the analyzed outlets, as

in fact did occur in the case of _Eldiario.es_ in news items and the positioning of

PP political spokespeople. This fact is due to the news items from _Eldiario.es_ having mostly agency authorship.


10 A firm providing tax, legal, audit, and advisory services in mergers and acquisitions,

restructuring, risk consulting, and business consulting.


Of the 38 reportages without direct reproduction of interested sources, 33 had nominal

authorship, 4 from the outlet itself, and 1 from an agency [11] (Graph 27).


If we compare the data in Graph 27 with those on authorship type in the total reportages

(Graph 20), the percentages are very similar. This is because the number of interested sources in reportages is not significant, so the results for non-interested sources in reportages are extrapolatable to the total of this journalistic genre, which is important when assessing the results of the reportages in relation to the research

objectives: non-interested sources, whose majority are reportages with nominal authorship,

give greater weight in the qualitative analysis to the reportages because in these are the

journalists who would seek to influence the political agenda. If these journalists tend to use

multiple sources and to act as a counterpower, they can also be related to some of the

data journalism values we wish to study.


11 That EUROPA PRESS published a reportage with multiple sources and interpretive charge (unit of analysis

117) has been a noteworthy fact given that agencies do not usually publish reportages. However, this

single exception from _El Mundo_ is nonetheless a minority that does not alter the general rule.


In this regard, _Eldiario.es_ published 13 reportages with these characteristics, _Elconfidencial.com_

12, _El Mundo_ 7, and _El País_ 6 (Graph 28).


If we compare these data with the percentage of reportages by outlet (Graph 20),

we see that the percentage differences are -3 points in _Eldiario.es_, +0.35 points in

_Elconfidencial.com_, -0.49 in _El País_, and +2.14 in _El Mundo_.


Of the 38 reportages without reproduction of interested sources, 21 used multiple

sources and 5 used the transparency portal—national, regional, or local. The other 12 articles used

single sources for their reportages (Graph 29).


These figures show the relationships between the type of source and the type of authorship in

reportages: the greater the nominal authorship, the less reproduction of interested

sources, which is self-evident in the practice of journalism and worth noting in

this study, since otherwise we would detect an intentionality not consistent with

some journalism values we are investigating. Similarly, it can be

observed that the more nominal authorships there are, the greater the use of multiple sources.


None of the 21 reportages with multiple sources directly reproduces interested

sources, and they represent 55.26% of reportages that do not directly reproduce

interested sources, of which 95.24% have nominal authorship and 4.76% have agency authorship.


The sole article using multiple sources with agency authorship is from EUROPA PRESS,

published by _El Mundo_ on October 23, 2015 under the title "Ahora Madrid, PSOE y C's

publicarán sus bienes, recogidos ya por el Ayuntamiento, mientras el PP optaría por otro

modelo" (EP, 2015c). This article is notable for its exceptional character: we

noted earlier that agencies are not usually authors of reportages. In

this publication, EP based itself on declarations by Ciudadanos, Ahora Madrid, and

PSOE deputies to announce the publication of "the declarations that are kept in a safe

in the City Hall, with the necessary removal of any information that violates the

Data Protection Law." The reportage refers back to earlier declarations from the

same political groups, adding the most recent ones from the PP in order to lay out the possible

forms these asset declarations would take, temporally contextualizing the

matter between the electoral promises of the May regional elections that year and the general

elections of December 20. The interpretive and analytical charge of the article, with the use of

multiple sources, led us to register it as a reportage.


**VI.2.2.1. Qualitative analysis of reportages**


Of the 5 reportages published by _El País_ during the analysis period, the pieces of

investigative journalism produced by Elena G. Sevillano in July 2015 are those that

most clearly show the consequences of the inadequacies of the Transparency Law. In an

article titled "Casi el 30% de peticiones al portal de transparencia se quedan sin respuesta"

(Sevillano, 2015a), now investigative reporter at _El País_ and then writer on

environmental and health topics, she criticized the failures to respond to public

information requests on the national portal. Another reportage by this journalist exposed how the

Ministry of Health concealed conflicts of interest of the committee that drafted the

National Strategic Plan for Addressing Hepatitis C, while in another she flagged the

parliamentary clashes over this issue. Although through this journalist we see how

_El País_ addressed topics similar to the other outlets, which by then already had data

journalism teams, the rest of the reportages with nominal authorship and multiple sources

were used as political weapons in the Catalan elections of September and the

general elections of December, not deviating an iota from the outlet's customary editorial line.


The reportage of September 21 titled "La ley de transparencia de Mas mantiene opacas

las donaciones" (Güell & Vidal, 2015) sought to counter the resonance of Artur

Mas's declarations about the Catalan transparency law as "one of the most complete and

demanding in the world." The other nominal-authorship reportage from _El País_ with multiple

sources was published on December 16 under the title "Los partidos se vuelcan en el voto

de las mujeres, que suman el 62% de los indecisos" (Junquera & Marcos, 2015), in which

transparency is a tangential topic for contextualizing the gender policies developed

by each of the parties in their programmatic content. In this regard, N. Junquera and

J. Marcos equated in a couple of lines the transparency proposals of the five major

parties heading to elections on December 20, before developing a very

complete article on programmatic differences in gender policies.


Of the nominal-authorship reportages with multiple sources from _El Mundo_, only one

shares characteristics of political weaponization according to the outlet's editorial line, as

shown by the article of December 17 by Antonio Moreno (2015) titled

"Colau aumenta la subvención al memorial a los caídos en 1714," which attempts to link the

political formation of the mayor of Barcelona with Catalan independentists through

a subsidy to an association that, among its functions, sought to "preserve the memory of
the Catalan patriots who fell" three centuries ago. To do so, Moreno contextualized the

subsidies in a climate of political uncertainty around Podemos and its confluences

ahead of the December 20 elections, citing sources from various political parties

to link the subsidy to a policy pursued by Catalan independentist parties and

giving weight to the statements made against it by Ciudadanos representatives.


The rest of the _El Mundo_ reportages clearly reflect an intention to place in

public opinion problems surrounding transparency without needing to follow the

editorial line of the outlet. Such was the case of the reportage of October 1, 2015 titled "¿Se le

puede regalar un velero de 50.000 euros a Don Juan Carlos?" (Terrasa, 2015), which

breaks down the transparency law and criticizes practices of the Spanish monarchy that would run counter

to the spirit of this law. The same occurred with the articles "El nuevo negocio de la

transparencia" (De la Torre, 2015), "Transparencia con pegas" (Treceño, 2015), and "El auditor

avisa desde 2013 del descontrol en los gastos de Sáez" (Salvador, 2015), published on

October 1, October 11, and December 18, 2015 respectively: these are reportages that

contextualize very well the problems of lack of transparency in various public

bodies regardless of whether their content affects the outlet's editorial line.


In the reportages with nominal authorship and multiple sources from _Elconfidencial.com_, the

intention of positioning transparency as a fundamental topic on the media

agenda is evident. Articles such as those by Ana Gómez (2015a, 2015b) titled "Lo que

nunca saldrá a la luz pese a la Ley de Transparencia" and "Los nuevos Ejecutivos de Madrid

intentan ponerse las pilas con la transparencia," of July 20 and August 4, 2015

respectively, are pieces that through their multiple sources give resonance to

declarations from CIVIO, Access Info Europe, Transparencia Internacional, and the

Transparency Council. All of this in contexts where political and institutional spokespeople such as

the mayor of Madrid, Manuela Carmena (Ahora Madrid), or the president of the regional government of

the Community of Madrid, Cristina Cifuentes (PP), are central to the reportages.


In the first article by Ana Gómez, the journalist criticizes the rejection of information

requests to public entities while promoting resolutions by the Transparency

Council, which urges them to respond. In the second reportage, Gómez extols the

stated intention or political will in the speeches of the regional and local governments of

Madrid while amplifying the declarations of Helen Darbishire and positions the

Transparencia Internacional ranking, all in the case of the two governmental entities

cited which are also political adversaries.


This positioning of voices favorable to transparency in contexts of multiple sources

was also seen in the reportage by data journalist Daniele Grasso (2015), titled "RTVE

elude al Consejo de Transparencia y oculta las facturas de Eurovisión," which presents

step by step how the public entity has managed to circumvent the Transparency Law and

not respond to a public information request, also evidencing the inadequacy of

the law for not complying with resolutions handed down by the Transparency Council instructing it to

publish the requested data. Similarly, the reportage by Carlos Sánchez titled

"Rebelión interna en el INE: un sindicato pone en solfa las prácticas del presidente" gives

voice to an INE union confronting the opacity of this public institution.


As part of positioning transparency values with the general public, a

reportage from _Elconfidencial.com_ signed by Kike Marín (2015) under the title "La FIFA acaba

con la impunidad de Villar, algo que no se ha hecho nunca en España" prompted the

tracking of cases of opacity and corruption by the president of the Spanish Football

Federation, Ángel María Vilar, to criticize Spain's inaction in the face of this type of

opaque behavior:


"…is being investigated for the alleged purchase of votes in the

awarding of the World Cups to Russia 2018 and Qatar 2022. The Bilbao lawyer has an

open file for refusing to testify in this entire process before prosecutor Michael Garcia.

The procedure is now in the hands of the dispute resolution chamber of the

supreme body of European football." (Marín, 2015)


In the _Eldiario.es_ reportages with nominal authorship and multiple sources, institutional

opacity in the government and the monarchy is criticized. Although these criticisms continue to support the

editorial line of the outlet, voice was given to sources that served as informational contrast in an

environment of oversaturation of news with interested sources—very evident in the case of

the news items from this native digital, as already seen in previous sections. Thus

_Eldiario.es_ gave voice to sources such as the then-president of the Transparency Council,

Esther Arizmendi, the RTVE Castilla-La Mancha workers, and the UN Sustainable Development

Goals (SDGs) in 3 of its reportages.


In another, _Eldiario.es_ criticizes the non-publication of public expenses for the coronation of

Felipe VI, while in an article jointly signed by Jaron Rowan and Pedro Jiménez

(2015b), the cultural programmatic content of the 5 main parties was broken down

ahead of the December 20 general elections to show how consistent they are

with their programs in using transparency as a political banner. This reportage is a clear

example of how all political parties incorporated transparency as part of their

discourse, as well as of the interest of outlets with data journalists in positioning it as a

fundamental topic in public opinion. In this regard, _Eldiario.es_ only identified the electoral program of Podemos as consistent with the cultural and transparency policies that the

purple party claimed to defend before public opinion:


"The word transparency bursts in with force, the exchange of files continues to be confused with

piracy, and the cultural industries seem inevitable, despite the precariousness… In

general terms, PODEMOS presents a conciliatory program… Transparency,

good practices, and accountability are central elements of

this party's cultural program." (Rowan & Jiménez, 2015b)


Although this reportage does not go against the outlet's editorial line in praising Podemos,

it actually meets parameters shared by reportages from another outlet with a

different editorial line: _Elconfidencial.com_.


In this regard, of the two reportages from _Elconfidencial.com_ with own authorship—both

signed by the native digital's data unit, Elconfidencial.lab—one used as its sole source

the electoral programs of political parties, published on December 10 under the

title "Así son las propuestas en transparencia para el 20D: nuestro voto, a Podemos"

(Elconfidencial.lab, 2015a). The article, published on the day the transparency law entered into force, highlighted how its values have entered Spanish political life forcefully by being reflected in the electoral programs for the coming legislature.


Among other things, Elconfidencial.lab tallied the common proposals of all political

parties and highlighted three that mentioned reforming the law and improving the portal, the creation

of a lobbying register, and the adoption of a sanctions regime. In this regard, according to this

data unit, Podemos went beyond the other formations by proposing to reform the commercial register website,

create a database of contracts and bids, and publish the donors of political parties who contribute more than 5,000 euros per year:


"If in quantitative terms Ciudadanos and PSOE lead the field (81 and 80 mentions of the concept

'transparency' in their programs, respectively, compared to 37 for Podemos, 33 for the PP and 26

for Unidad Popular), does the number of times the political buzzword of the moment appears coincide with the

quality of its proposals? Let us see… The party led by Pablo Iglesias has

presented the most ambitious program on transparency." (Elconfidencial.lab,

2015a)


Another article by Elconfidencial.lab that used a single source was published on

September 2 under the title "Descubre cuántos viajes (oficiales) al extranjero ha realizado el

Gobierno" (Elconfidencial.lab, 2015b). In it, a database created by

the data unit of _Elconfidencial.com_ was used, built from data provided by several ministries

in response to multiple public information access requests sent to all Spanish

ministries through the Transparency Portal, requesting the list of official trips abroad by each minister. This has been a perfect example of a data journalism piece that meets all the fundamental aspects developed in the theoretical framework of this study and, for purposes of this content analysis, is another example of the effort of these data journalists to position values related to

transparency as a fundamental topic in public opinion.


The two reportages without direct source reproduction and with own authorship from _Eldiario.es_

were each based on single sources derived from the transparency portal, both on dates

close to the entry into force of the transparency law. One article, published on December 8

under the title "Cantabria no está preparada para aplicar la Ley de Transparencia a

dos días de su entrada en vigor" (_Eldiario.es_, 2015b), criticized the lack of preparation of this

autonomous community to independently set up the regional transparency portal. Another reportage of December 11 under the title "RTVCM destina un 11% menos a

sueldos de directivos desde septiembre" was based on information published on the regional

transparency portal of Castilla-La Mancha to carry out a comparative study between the

salaries of RTVE Castilla-La Mancha managers before the new regional government that

started its term in May.


**VI.2.3. Opinion**


Of the 27 opinion articles, just over half were published by native digital

outlets, leaving behind the predominance of native digitals over traditional outlets seen in other

genres. In fact, _Eldiario.es_, the outlet with the most publications in news and reportages, had the

fewest opinion articles: only 4 publications. The outlet with the greatest number of

opinion articles was _Elconfidencial.com_ (10), followed by _El Mundo_ (7) and _El País_ (6).


If we observe the behavior of publications over time (Graph 31) we

realize that in the first month all outlets published at least one opinion

article, with _Eldiario.es_ having the most by publishing double the others: 2. However,

in the second period of the sample (Month 2) the only outlet that continued publishing was _El_

_Mundo_, with just 1 article, with the drop in the general trend between the first and

second period being due to the other outlets.


In month 3, _Elconfidencial.com_ and _El Mundo_ had 1 article each, with _El País_ and _Eldiario.es_ doubling this

amount with 2 articles each. In the fourth period

_Elconfidencial.com_ and _El País_ published 2 each, while in month 5 there were only 3

articles: 2 from _Elconfidencial.com_ and 1 from _El Mundo_. In month 6, _Elconfidencial.com_ published

4 articles, _El Mundo_ 3, and _El País_ 1.

|Outlet|Month 1|Month 2|Month 3|Month 4|Month 5|Month 6|
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
|_Eldiario.es_ |2 |0 |2 |0 |0 |0 |
|_Elconfidencial.com_ |1 |0 |1 |2 |2 |4 |
|_El Mundo_ |1 |1 |1 |0 |1 |3 |
|_El País_ |1 |0 |2 |2 |0 |1 |


The total data for all the journalistic genres analyzed in the sample show what is typical in

media outlets: more news articles are published, followed by reportages, and then, to a much lesser

extent, opinion pieces and interviews.


**VI.2.3.1. Editorials**


As for editorials, they are the most important articles of the opinion genre and, in the

case of traditional outlets, are usually labeled as such in their publications. However,

native digital outlets do not usually publish editorials or label them as such, which

is because their opinion articles tend to appear in their blog sections or assimilated external blogs. In these cases, publications signed by the outlets' directors

are usually considered editorials: in the case of _Elconfidencial.com_ this is Nacho Cardero and

in _Eldiario.es_, Ignacio Escolar.


The outlet with the most editorials in the sample was _El Mundo_, with 3 publications of this type, which

represent 42.85% of its total opinion articles. It is followed by _Elconfidencial.com_

and _Eldiario.es_, with 1 editorial each and representing 10% and 40% of their total

articles respectively. _El País_ had no editorial, which is a very

important fact to take into account in the analysis and sets it apart from the other outlets in the sample.


Of the 3 _El Mundo_ editorials, one was published on June 26 under the title "La regulación

del 'lobby' es una saludable iniciativa de transparencia institucional" (_El Mundo_, 2015a),

while the other two were published in December under the headlines "La endogamia en los

partidos frustra la regeneración" (_El Mundo_, 2015b), on December 6, and "Un voto para

una España unida, plural y regenerada" (_El Mundo_, 2015c), on December 19. The June article

marks the outlet's editorial line with respect to political formations by asserting

that "The initiative to regulate lobbying included in the investiture pact for the Community

of Madrid between the PP and Ciudadanos is a good example of the healthy effects for

democratic regeneration being achieved with its agreements by the formation of Albert

Rivera." In the December 6 editorial, the lack of openness of political parties

to society is blamed for "the scarcity of transparency" as well as "the emergence of cases of

corruption and nepotism," issuing a call to halt the professionalization of

politics. On December 19, _El Mundo_ devotes its editorial to the future Government so that "the

fight against corruption and the regeneration of democratic life" is its priority,

thereby encouraging the fulfillment of "citizens' right to transparency" as part of this

regeneration.


In all its editorials, we see how _El Mundo_ not only uses transparency to support its

editorial line, but also how it attempts to influence traditional parties to halt the

momentum of emerging political forces such as Podemos and its confluences, which it does not

mention in any of its editorials. However, it is striking how it does cite

Ciudadanos as part of this democratic regeneration, urging the PP and PSOE to follow its

example. In this regard, it is clear how in the outlet's editorial line, transparency and good

governance are a tool for influencing politics.


As for _Elconfidencial.com_, we see how in its editorial of November 23, under the title

"Iñaki Urdangarin no lee a Séneca (o por qué Zarzuela abjura de un pacto con la Fiscalía),"

Nacho Cardero (2015) does justice to the outlet's editorial line by praising the

monarchical institution through Felipe VI, whom he identifies as the architect of the then recently

approved Transparency Law. However, it is this vision of Felipe VI as a key element

of democratic regeneration in Spain that the director of _Elconfidencial.com_ uses to

attempt to influence the Nóos case, highlighting the possible consequences of not allowing

Urdangarin to be properly prosecuted, among which is the undermining of

Felipe VI's image as a symbol of democratic regeneration. In this case, the editorial from

_Elconfidencial.com_ has sought to influence politics through the transparency and good

governance that is part of the democratic regeneration linked to the new representative

of the monarchical institution.


In the case of _Eldiario.es_, the editorial of September 18 by Ignacio Escolar (2015) under the

title "Las cuentas de _Eldiario.es_ en su tercer aniversario," although it is a

corporate communication, if we take into consideration the lack of information about the accounts of Spanish outlets shared with their readers and society in general, it can be classified as an exercise in

transparency. Although it is not surprising that the outlet with the most publications in the total

articles across all genres on transparency and good governance should try to use the topic to

promote itself, it is nonetheless notable that there are not more editorials seeking to support the

editorial line of the outlet through transparency. In fact, the other three opinion

articles from this outlet treat transparency as a secondary topic in subjects of energy policy

(2 articles) and media policy (1 article).


**VI.2.3.2. Opinion articles and notable examples**


In the _Eldiario.es_ articles from July under the headlines "La persecución del

Gobierno a la energía solar es ya obsesiva" (Morales de Labra, 2015a) and "El control político

de los medios de comunicación" (Sanclemente, 2015), published on July 12 and 16

respectively, transparency is used to criticize institutional opacity toward

public government policies. In the first article, Jorge Morales focuses on the

energy policies pursued by the government that negatively affected

energy self-sufficiency, criticizing the opacity of electricity bills and

governmental inaction in the face of such lack of transparency. The second article criticizes governmental

opacity regarding subsidies to private media outlets and the purchase of institutional

advertising in these outlets to influence their editorial line, calling for the use of the new political landscape that "offers a magnificent opportunity to

eradicate the practices of obscurantism and media manipulation."


In the other opinion article from _Eldiario.es_, published on August 29 under the title "¿Quién

iba a decir que un simple panel solar iba a destapar las vergüenzas del sector eléctrico?,"

Jorge Morales (2015b) again attacks public energy policies, this time centering the article on the political integration of domestic electricity self-consumption, for which

"objectivity, transparency and future vision" would be needed.


In the case of _Elconfidencial.com_, the majority of opinion articles reinforce the

editorial line of the outlet, although there are more diverse voices and even those of transparency

activists. An example of transparency activism published in this outlet without

deviating from the editorial line is represented by Javier Martín, from the Fundación Compromiso y

Transparencia. Of his two articles, the one published on July 15 under the title "José

Folgado, el político que sonrojó a los empresarios" (Martín, 2015a), made an ode to the politician

at the helm of Red Eléctrica España as an example of institutional transparency, asserting

that "a politician who came to the presidency of a company with public capital (Red Eléctrica)

by virtue of party membership has revealed himself as the paradigm of good governance in

our country." The other article, published on September 19 under the title "A propósito de la

financiación de las fundaciones políticas" (Martín, 2015b), uses the report by the Fundación

Compromiso y Transparencia on the funding of foundations linked to political parties

to denounce the opacity of all political formations. The author's political tendency, very consistent with the editorial line of the outlet, was seen not only in this equating of

all political formations as opaque, but in the fact that he highlighted the case of

corruption surrounding Convergencia Democrática and the measures taken by Ciudadanos in

the context of an electoral campaign for the Catalan elections.


Another example of a publication that praises transparency and good governance without deviating from

the editorial line of _Elconfidencial.com_ was the article titled "Carmena ya no quiere a

Podemos," in which Fran Carrillo (2015) presented Ahora Madrid as an example of

transparency of the new politics while lambasting Podemos as "populist" and using other

epithets. The article sought to siphon votes from the Madrid formation linked to

Podemos in the December general elections, presenting a supposed distancing

between both political platforms. However, articles such as the one published on

September 24 under the title "Encuentros en la tercera fase con los concejales de plataformas

ciudadanas" (Adsuara, 2015), do not take such a marked political stance in

Spanish politics. In this example, any citizen platform that has reached the

institutions of political power is praised and urged to go beyond the transparency linked to

the fight against corruption:


"We must overcome the concept of transparency, which has unfortunately become fashionable,

very closely linked to and referenced in the fight against corruption, and speak instead of

open data, which has a far broader scope. Once we overcome the epidemic of corruption we have

suffered, the question will no longer be whether a politician or public

administrator is honest (since we should start from the assumption that they are and not presuppose

the contrary), but whether they are competent. If Public Administrations open their data,

the media and citizens will be able to find out what they do with our money and

judge whether they use it well or badly; whether they invest it properly, or whether they squander it."

(Adsuara, 2015)


In this way, the opinion articles of _Elconfidencial.com_ evidence a tendency

detected earlier in news and reportages: despite the editorial line of the outlet, transparency and good governance form such an important part of the native digital's content

that it can even be reflected in articles that might seem to go against the

editorial line of the outlet and in some cases even modify it. In this regard, articles of

evident partisan political charge such as "Fantasmas y enchufados en Andalucía" by Javier

Caraballo (2015), contrast with others such as the one published by the activist platform Xnet

(2015) under the title "Protejamos a los denunciantes y alertadores," in which an

analogy was made with the Snowden case to assert that in Spain "the people who denounce corruption are persecuted rather than protected," later advocating the following:


"The protection of whistleblowers/alerters is a struggle to defend the collective work

of transparency and denunciation and not a way of creating a society of informers

as authoritarian governments have often done." (Xnet, 2015)


Two more evident examples of this contrasting opinion in _Elconfidencial.com_ arise in the

context of the December 20 electoral campaign. The first is the article titled "El

Ibex ante el 20-D: temor a un Gobierno débil y terror a un cambio generacional," published on

December 14, 2015 with the byline of José Antonio Navas (2015). The article is a clear

political apology against Podemos, since according to the author the purple formation represents the

"economic regression in a recovering Spain." The transparency discussed

here is corporate and is used as a weapon against the Santander group, mentioned as

an example not to follow in business practices: the Spanish business community should give way to

new generations, just as the political leadership should with Ciudadanos so as to

curb the momentum of Podemos. It is an article that contrasts sharply with one by Elena Herrero

Beaumont (2015) titled "La transparencia del nuevo poder," published on December 12

of 2015. That article, which forms part of the El Rincón de la Transparencia section of

_Elconfidencial.com_, is an apology for new conceptions of power represented by the

city councils of Madrid and Barcelona: "the new forms of power, linked to

transparency and participation, augur a priori positive scenarios for society as a

whole."


Despite this pluralism in the opinion articles of _Elconfidencial.com_, those in

keeping with its editorial line are still in the majority, as with the last article to be cited

from this outlet. In it, published on December 17 under the title "Enchufismo, marca

España," Javier Caraballo (2015) used critiques of the opacity of Spanish political and institutional

life to make an analysis of its causes in which nepotism, in the case of

Andalusia, is clearly linked to the PSOE of Susana Díaz.


Of the 4 opinion articles from _El Mundo_ that are not editorials, 1 was "Letters to the editor," [12]

published on December 11, in which one of the 3 citizens who wrote to this

traditional outlet, David Pérez Tallón, expressed the following about the citizen demand

for the transparency championed by political parties in their electoral campaigns that

year:


"It is curious that during campaigns they proclaim, as an electoral appeal, that they will not raise

taxes or will even lower them, when anyone who looks a little deeper will realize that what

12 We draw on "Las cartas del director como género periodístico" (Córdova, 2011), which classifies them as

part of the macro-persuasive genre to which opinion columns and editorials would belong.


truly concerns us and what we citizens need is transparency,

that they clarify for us what they are going to do with our money, whether in greater or lesser measure the

amount we must contribute at any given moment to the public coffers." (Pérez, Lomas & Gómez,

2015)


In this way, through editorials on transparency and this letter to the editor, _El_

_Mundo_ has succeeded in incorporating into its editorial line citizens' demands for transparency

and possible responses to its failures in Spanish institutional life, in the context of

a possible political change ahead of the general elections of December 20, 2015. All of

this implies not only the attempt to influence politics through transparency and good

governance as part of democratic regeneration, but also demonstrates how in its

opinion articles, _El Mundo_ has attempted to influence the very public policies on

transparency and good governance affecting the development of data journalism, which is seen more clearly

in the article of August 6 titled "'Lobbies' y transparencia: una combinación difícil"

(Entrena, 2015b).


In this publication, Rafel Entrena (2015a) celebrates the intent of Decree 171/2015, of July 28,

of the Departament de Justícia of the Catalan Generalitat, as "a step forward in the

transparency of the public sector and the prevention of possible situations of conflicts of

interest and corruption." However, the columnist develops a sharp critique throughout

his publication regarding the effectiveness of the decree, since "if what is intended is to give

transparency to the legitimate and legal actions of entities," this will not be achieved with "merely

providing for the formalization of the application registration on the applicant's own initiative with no more

incentive" than publicly declaring that one is an interest group. In this regard, for Entrena

the logical course would be to incentivize registration in the lobbying register with measures such as "facilitating

their participation in regulatory initiatives or preferential access to senior officials or

parliamentary groups."


In another article from _El Mundo_, Elisa De La Nuez addressed the conflicts of interest of the

experts appointed by the Ministry of Health to draft the National Plan against

Hepatitis C by publishing on August 21 "Honestidad intelectual y conflicto de intereses" (De

La Nuez, 2015). In this publication, the opacity with which the experts
